Within — Wisdom Library

Quotes from saints and mystics with reflections connected to meditation, inquiry, silence and
conscious living.

1

Quote

“What you seek is seeking you.”

Author

Rumi

Tradition

Sufi

Reflection

This reflection invites us to look within rather than searching for answers in the
outer world. When we pause in silence or observe our inner experience, we begin
to notice the awareness that receives thoughts, emotions, and sensations.
Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.

“Happiness is your nature. — reflecting on self.”

Author

Ramana Maharshi

Tradition

Advaita

Reflection

This reflection invites us to look within rather than searching for answers in the
outer world. When we pause in silence or observe our inner experience, we begin
to notice the awareness that receives thoughts, emotions, and sensations.
Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.

outer world. When we pause in silence or observe our inner experience, we begin
to notice the awareness that receives thoughts, emotions, and sensations.
Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.

Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.

Tradition

Advaita

Reflection

This reflection invites us to look within rather than searching for answers in the
outer world. When we pause in silence or observe our inner experience, we begin
to notice the awareness that receives thoughts, emotions, and sensations.
Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.

to notice the awareness that receives thoughts, emotions, and sensations.
Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.

Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.

“Truth is high, but higher still is truthful living. — reflecting on
compassion.”

Author

Guru Nanak

Tradition

Sikh

Reflection

This reflection invites us to look within rather than searching for answers in the
outer world. When we pause in silence or observe our inner experience, we begin
to notice the awareness that receives thoughts, emotions, and sensations.
Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.

Buddhist

Reflection

This reflection invites us to look within rather than searching for answers in the
outer world. When we pause in silence or observe our inner experience, we begin
to notice the awareness that receives thoughts, emotions, and sensations.
Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.

to notice the awareness that receives thoughts, emotions, and sensations.
Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.

outer world. When we pause in silence or observe our inner experience, we begin
to notice the awareness that receives thoughts, emotions, and sensations.
Practices such as inquiry and quiet sitting reveal that the wisdom spoken by
mystics is not theoretical but directly discoverable in our own experience. Living
with this attention gradually brings clarity, compassion, and a deeper sense of
connection with life.
